<div id="review_187314204" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187314204" />
    <a title="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog"><img alt="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583236251p2/3575839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187314204?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)" href="/user/show/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog">Suzanne (Under the Covers Book blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=va-va-voom-vampires">va-va-voom-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=genre-paranormal-romance">genre-paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3575839-suzanne-under-the-covers-book-blog?shelf=demons">demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187314204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11522114615344379546">I was so ready for Gideon's book after reading Jacob's, he is the oldest of the Demons, but of course still mega hot, so don't fear there are no saggy man bums and wrinkly...other things, as the eldest, an Ancient he is the most powerful demon, but he has been living a solitary life as a self infliced punishment for the wrongs he committed in his long past. That is until Legna, the Demon King Noah's empath sister comes along and totally rocks his world. <br/><br/>I wanted to like this much more then I act</span>
  <span id="freeText11522114615344379546" style="display:none">I was so ready for Gideon's book after reading Jacob's, he is the oldest of the Demons, but of course still mega hot, so don't fear there are no saggy man bums and wrinkly...other things, as the eldest, an Ancient he is the most powerful demon, but he has been living a solitary life as a self infliced punishment for the wrongs he committed in his long past. That is until Legna, the Demon King Noah's empath sister comes along and totally rocks his world. <br /><br />I wanted to like this much more then I actually did I preferred Jacob's book, mainly as I didn't warm up to Gideon. He was at intially too distant, cold and arrogant (but not in a sexy way)and although he did warm up and let his emotions out eventually I was stuck firmly in the <i>meh</i> camp complete with big cheery fire and toasted marshmallows. Another thing as well which kinda bugged me, the one of the big reasons he felt he didn't deserve Legna was because he encouraged and helped commit an atrocity and he feels intense guilt and regret about it and I was thinking YES! You should feel guilt and regret you committed geonicide, granted it was 900 years ago but still the Druids are no less dead. I mean he was forgiven but it niggled me.<br /><br />I did like Legna though, probably more then Gideon, she was a good character and I liked that she wasn't scared to tell off all the strong alpha males surrounding her. <br /><br />What I liked most about this book and what earnt it most of the stars was the progression of the main plot regaring the Hunters and Necromancers that hunt not only the Demons but all the other Nightwalker races. An act of betrayal with in the Demon ranks maked the Necromancers even more dangerous in this book and although it is obvious who it is, it was still a good twist. We also see a little bit more of the other Nightwalker races when the Lycanthrope queen Siena and the Vampire prince Damien show up, we especially learn more about the Lycanthropes and I like that the shifters are a little different in these books. <br /><br />I did like this book, a few places had my eyes rolling and I have mentioned my Gideon issues, but I will be on to the next book as I do like the series.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11522114615344379546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18021917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18021917" />
    <a title="Christel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/655568-christel"><img alt="Christel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1234459248p2/655568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18021917?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christel" href="/user/show/655568-christel">Christel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">paranormal romance readers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christel by: </span>
      amazon.com
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/655568-christel?shelf=jacquelyn-frank">jacquelyn-frank</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18021917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14920927882252409747">This is the second book in the series.<br/><br/>Gideon is an Ancient, a healer, who has taken his duties seriously for the 1000 years he has been alive. He is known for great wisdom and is well respected among his race of demons. But he is vulnerable to the primitive desires of his race during the time of the hallowed moon, Samhaim. Nine years ago , he lost his composure with his king's baby sister, Magdelegna. He berated himself for his weakness for Legna is but a mere child to his age. He exiled himself</span>
  <span id="freeText14920927882252409747" style="display:none">This is the second book in the series.<br /><br />Gideon is an Ancient, a healer, who has taken his duties seriously for the 1000 years he has been alive. He is known for great wisdom and is well respected among his race of demons. But he is vulnerable to the primitive desires of his race during the time of the hallowed moon, Samhaim. Nine years ago , he lost his composure with his king's baby sister, Magdelegna. He berated himself for his weakness for Legna is but a mere child to his age. He exiled himself because of this.<br />Magdelegna is only about 250 years old, an emerging Elder inher society. She remembers the incident with Gideon nine years ago and she feels shamed and betrayed by the Ancient one. She is a mind demon who is undergoing changes that she is not really sure of. The changes started nine years ago. She is far more advanced in doing things than a Demon should be at her age.<br />They both realize that they are meant for each other, mates for eternity. But Gideon must regain her trust to gain her love. And Legna must come to terms with her past in more ways than one.<br />This to me was the best of the 2 novels I have read so far. The beginning was slow because the reader has to learn the backstory in regards to Gideon's and Legna's romance. Other characters from the first book are carried over, Noah, the Demon King, Jacob and Isabella, the Enforcer and his half-Druid mate, Elijah, the Warrior captain of the demons. Plus new characters, Siena, the Queen of the Lycanthropes and Damien, Prince of the Vampires.<br />I cannot wait till I can read the next book, Elijah, about the Warrior captain and Siena, Queen of the Lycanthropes, plus the others in the series. Quite interesting take on the all of the Nightwalker species.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14920927882252409747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8318129199833703376">I did read the first in this series <b>
  <i>Jacob</i>
</b>, and felt it was a decent start to a new series. So, when I found a cheap used copy of this one, I figured what the heck?<br/><br/>Ugh, I wish I hadn't bothered. I didn't even finish it, and I just don't NOT finish a book. It's only happened less than a handful of times.<br/><br/>I felt like it took way too long to get to the story for this book. It seemed like a quarter of the book was spent rehashing the first one. And not even creatively. The dialogue felt so forced </span>
  <span id="freeText8318129199833703376" style="display:none">I did read the first in this series <b>
  <i>Jacob</i>
</b>, and felt it was a decent start to a new series. So, when I found a cheap used copy of this one, I figured what the heck?<br /><br />Ugh, I wish I hadn't bothered. I didn't even finish it, and I just don't NOT finish a book. It's only happened less than a handful of times.<br /><br />I felt like it took way too long to get to the story for this book. It seemed like a quarter of the book was spent rehashing the first one. And not even creatively. The dialogue felt so forced and obvious, I thought I was reading a bad Soap Opera's script or something. <br /><br />I got more than half way through it, and never once could connect to the main characters. Or, should I say, who the main characters are supposed to be. There's so much involving other characters, I felt Gideon and Legna, were almost side story. <br /><br />Not sure if I could make myself read the next one. But who knows... I can be a glutton for punishment.</span>

The Love Making is Clinical like a GYN visit to the DR. what was that about?   <span id="freeText1093535049364668957" style="display:none">I wish it was a way to give this book ZERO STARS thats how bad it is. It starts and finishes very slow. The Love Making is Clinical like a GYN visit to the DR. what was that about? No Romance at all between Gideon and Magdelegna The dialogue between the characters were mediocre at best and the arguments that Medelegna always started with Gideon came out of nowhere they were stupid and childish with no bases and insignificant. For Great writers of the paranormal I suggest you try Kerrelyn Sparks, Lara Adrian or J R Ward these are the best in this field of writing and they all write in their own unique style!!!!!! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11029269857642964773">This is a different story than the first part.<br/><br/>Like Gideon and his brutal honesty and directness, his logic.<br/><br/>Legna behaves like many typical female characters.<br/><br/>However, the way that these characters influencing each other is a great, refreshing and healthy.<br/><br/>Yes, they wanted to change some things on one another, but nothing too much, nothing terrible and unreasonable. Concessions were minimal, perfected them - this is perhaps the healthiest compromise the healthiest person I met in the books.</span>

<div id="review_221732276" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221732276" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4653153-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1292245515p2/4653153.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221732276?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/4653153-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer221732276&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221732276" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9158367398426533636">this is the 2nd time i've read this book.i picked it up again because i didn't think i had read it all the way through the first time.then i realized that i had,in fact, read the whole thing.i just couldn't remember it.that should say a lot about this book.<br/>This book is a cross between Sherrilyn Kenyon’s Dream Hunter series and Christine Feehan’s Carpathian series. I feel like she tried to capture the relationships in Feehan’s books, like the possessiveness. Unfortunately, she took it to such a l</span>
  <span id="freeText9158367398426533636" style="display:none">this is the 2nd time i've read this book.i picked it up again because i didn't think i had read it all the way through the first time.then i realized that i had,in fact, read the whole thing.i just couldn't remember it.that should say a lot about this book.<br />This book is a cross between Sherrilyn Kenyon’s Dream Hunter series and Christine Feehan’s Carpathian series. I feel like she tried to capture the relationships in Feehan’s books, like the possessiveness. Unfortunately, she took it to such a level where it was just ridiculous. <br />She’d say things like ‘gee u r so wise. I am so tremendously lucky! Most girls get stuck w/ an insufferable, devious, underhanded snake of a man.’ And then he’d smile or laugh..&amp;I’m just like that wasn’t funny. &amp;then following that dumb and embarrassing comment he said ‘u will never bore me, Nelissuna. I can see that fact straight 2my soul’. First of all, what has she done thus far that would warrant a comment like that? She isn’t funny. she doesn’t do any outrageous, crazy, daring things. This is a pathetic rip-off of Christine Feehan books.She definitely tried to imitate the relationships in Christine’s books.<br />&amp;Gideon &amp;legna (&amp;btw could you find another spelling for that cause every time I read it I wanna say leg-na) go from barely tolerating each other to having ‘cute’ lil arguments that reminds me of somethin I’ve read before..Oh yeah! Gregori&amp; Savannah! (Dark Magic by Christine Feehan). I think she read Christine Feehan’s books and then immediately ran to her computer and started typing. This is blatantly copying someone else. She tried to run with it and then completely bombed.<br />&amp;molten mercury? that’s yet another thing you blatantly copied from Feehan. <br />&amp; basically I gathered that Gideon was actually being considerate when he chased that human girl cause he was seriously aroused cause of the full moon…or sum such nonsense that takes place every so often that makes guys wanna jump people. So Legna basically thanks the guy for going after this other girl. Nine years of pain suddenly vanishes because they become each other’s intended during a body scan..<br />Words can’t even begin to describe how dumb I think all this is.<br />1st of all Gideon didn’t know they were life mates until like a day ago. So 9 years ago he still went after the girl because he wanted to. He chose to leave you that night in the garden so it’s his fault he isn’t ‘getting any’-hint hint.<br />The main character got over things mighty quickly just because he entered her body..and not in the way you think. He was doing an internal scan which I can’t really explain cause I don’t really understand it.<br />&amp;just cause of that everything was forgotten.9 years of avoiding each other like the plague was totally forgotten for some dumb body scan that set their whole imprinting thing in motion.<br />The main character alternates from sounding like an old lady to a young girl. <br />@the beginning of the book Magdalegna came off as an old lady who was absurdly stuffy&amp; then other times she acted like a little kid, all sniffling and crying like a baby. Maybe there was a little split personality thing goin on here…<br />1 minute she’s calling him an insufferable, devious, underhanded snake of a man&amp; the next she’s sticking up for him to her brother saying he isn’t a ‘manipulative monster’. Basically, this book is one big ‘ol contradiction. She’s all over the place with her feelings. She’s mad and hurt at the beginning of the book, and then she miraculously gets over it and basically jumps the guy. then she says she’s not ready so he gives her times &amp;then she jumps him again. Then she sticks up for him, then she’s back to jumping him.<br />Poor Gideon was probably getting a bunch of mixed signals.<br />Stuff that doesn’t make sense in this book-<br />Sentence from book-‘she was equally frustrated that all these troubles stood between them.’<br />Uh…wut troubles,exactly? Do explain, cause I’m just not seeing these troubles you speak of.<br />She’s the kind of girl who says ‘he was right,of course’ for everything.i just wanted to yell get it together girl &amp;get a freakin backbone! I mean she practically thanked him for almost having sex with this human.<br />‘you do not have enough experience working with these instinctual emotions. They are new,and,as you know, can be overwhelming. Until you learn to acknowledge them and integrate them into yourself, you are in danger of losing focus and control. I do not have to tell you how dangerous that is in a volatile situation.’ <br />Uh…HUH??? They’re just feelings. You don’t know what you’re feeling?!<br />None of this book made a lick of sense!<br />Here’s a lil tidbit from this book so you can see where I’m coming from….<br />‘She was his one true mate, his second half, the feminine side of himself that flourished on intuition and protective instincts. She was the side that turned calm before the battle so as to see to complete preparation for what was to come. She was center, focus, and everything moral that would guide his actions. She was the strategy and logic that would take him along the best course to victory while exercising caution for his own safety. She was mercy for those who would lie beaten at his feet, satisfying him with victory while sparing him the poisonous joy of killing when it was no longer needed. She was the peace and the light that would keep him from burdening himself with the heavy weight of taking a life, no matter how justified it was.<br />He was her one true mate, her second half. As she armed him, she felt him slipping deeply into her soul, becoming the masculine side of herself. This was the place within her that thrived on defending what was hers, the part that would mark her territory with the blood of her enemies if they dared cross the lines set before them. He became her sense of authority and righteousness, the part of her that was battle scarred and warrior skilled. He was her physical prowess, her devious cunning, and the part that would endure the pain and wounds of hell rather than see injustice done. He was the darkness and the conflict that kept her from becoming too complacent in the soft nature of peace, leaving herself open to the attack of those who were not so honorable in ideals as she would have them be.’<br />Confused? Are you scratching your head? Are you looking up off into space and thinking ‘what the h***?’ well, I did the exact same thing when I read this. when I first started reading the paragraph I thought it couldn’t possibly get more confusing/stupid. Boy was I wrong.it got more stupid the more I read. the last sentence really topped it all off. I don’t even think the author knew what she was talking about any more than us readers do.&amp;basically wut I gathered from that was that legna's gotta be wonder woman.<br />I almost fell asleep during their many speeches and explanations, conversations and private thoughts-basically the whole book. I couldn’t understand any of it. I heartily wished she would have just spoken in plain English! She almost bored me to tears. Let’s just say if you can’t go to sleep just crack this sucker open&amp; start reading. You’ll be snoozing soon, I can almost guarantee it. Particularly pgs. 158-166. <br />After Corrine was taken, they’re all talking about what 2 do &amp; what happens &amp;everything. &amp;Siena’s like as soon as u introduce me I’ll explain things &amp;I’m like skip the freakin introductions.sum1 was KIDNAPPED &amp;they’re all having idle chitchat. &amp;then ‘ol leg-na is like ‘I need time to rest. i have taxed myself.’ 1st of all who on this planet says ‘taxed myself.’ There again the author writes in a way that no1 really talks like.&amp; 2nd,sum1s life is on the line. This isn’t the time to worry about your ‘taxed self.’ So then Kane, Corrine’s mate is like we can’t afford that kind of time. &amp;she says he’s rite, give me 2hours.now idk about ne1 else but 2hours seems like a significant amount of time to leave someone hanging who’s been kidnapped. Usually u immediately run off 2 save them. &amp;after Corrine was saved I expected a little more reaction from the characters. I wanted to see her mate’s reaction and everything but she totally skipped that part. I mean, if you’re going to put the kidnapping in there you need to play it all the way through.<br />There are a lot of terms and stuff n here that flew right over my head. Actually, there were a lot of things I didn’t understand n here. Like all this talk of ‘body chemistry’ like Gideon would analyze and change Legna’s body chemistry. &amp;maybe it’s because I don’t understand that stuff but it just didn’t seem possible. <br />‘physiological’ and ‘psychological’ and ‘psyche’ was mentioned frequently. Pretty much every word that started with ‘psych’ was put into this book. It’s just something else that went completely over my head.<br />&amp;the sulfur smell when someone transports-why would you put that in here? How random is sulfur?! Could you possibly think of something else that smells more disgusting? Maybe roadkill. Garbage cans. Rotting fruit.<br />Wth was up w/ demons drinking zebra milk and sum yellow liquid from giraffes that i dont even wanna know where it comes from.<br />&amp;the whole ‘needleless transfusions’ ‘let me come into your body to assess the damages’ things were weird and disgusting. <br />&amp;I happened to be eating during the whole ‘Isabella blood placenta sticky body fluid thing’ so needless to say I was a little grossed out.<br />The whole ‘huntress’ thing, like u should help protect and defend, only hunt for what you need, only kill for survival and self-defense. It sounds like she’s trying to take the whole animalistic nature and instincts thing which is usually in a werewolf or vampire book. And demons aren’t animals…or ‘in tune’ with nature-like body, earth, fire and mind demons. I guess I just didn’t like her take on the whole demon, lycanthrope, and necromancer deal. <br />&amp;hair that moves is too stupid for me to even comprehend. Why on earth would you put such a ridiculous thing in ur book. I have to say, it isn’t as stupid as this other book I read where the girl had living hair, but it’s definitely right up there with it. &amp;i just knew that siena and elijah would end up together-which im not crazy about at all cause i didn't really care for siena.<br />i probably won't read their book cause i don't think i can put up with her hair that has a mind of its own that reaches out and wraps around peoples wrists to hold them close.it reminds me of that other book i read where the girls hair wrapped around the guys..neither regions.<br />do ppl really get their kicks from that stuff?!<br />and speaking about kicks,the love scenes,if you can even call them that, in this book was boring.like the first scene she's like undressing him or whatever,and i was about to fall asleep.you think stuff like that would wake you up a little,but it didn't.it had like the opposite effect.i wasn't interested at all.<br />This is one of those books where like every word is capitalized, signifying importance, when most of it didn’t even need to be capitalized.<br />Maybe it's a little hard to understand because it's the second book in the series and i haven't read the first one, but I found a lot of what they were talking about to be way over my head. <br />I felt completely stumped and confused and was constantly thinking ‘What??’ throughout this entire book. She makes the dialogue in here completely hard to understand. It’s like instead of just saying it plainly she finds the most complicated way to say something and then puts it in her book. &amp;the way characters speak is totally unreal. Maybe it sounded eloquent in her head but I can promise u nothing was even remotely eloquent in this book.<br />I think if I could sum this whole book up, I’d put just a big question mark. It was a rare thing when I actually understood what people were saying.<br />You either have to be really smart or dumb as a brick to write this. I still can’t decide which one this author is.<br />i'll explain-you either have to truly understand terms like 'body chemistry' 'physiology' 'psychology' 'psyche' or you have no idea what any of that means so you just stick it in your book trying to sound all intellectual when in fact you know nothing of what you're talking about.<br />the good thing is, the book got easier to understand as it got closer to the end.<br />this i realized upon finishing it, is one of those books where we end up not truly knowing the main charcter.we just don't get a true understanding of who she is.and what we do see we don't like.<br />it’s talk like this that brings up the disgusted face. <br />Its sickeningly sweet. &amp;I cant help but wonder-do people really talk like this? <br />–“I told you, my love, I am not going anywhere. I am here, right where I belong. My heart lives with your heart, my soul with your soul. I love you, Gideon. You have to start believing that, and believing that you deserve it.” “I will never deserve it,” he said roughly. “but I will endeavor to do so for the rest of my days. I love you, Neliss, as I have never loved in the whole of my life. You are my heart, my breath, my every thought and every aspiration. You are the true source of my power, because without you I am utterly powerless.”<br />Had I read this at the start of my romance reading days, I would have thought it was really sweet, but now that I’ve read quite a few things like this, I find it not to be sweet at all<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9158367398426533636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0Q1QCb6ezRzSFFphWS+uPJASYp4BIL3ZqpXBSsF5yFwwG8D5gmZBAzWtFRhjhZpvOE95WjDp1c+Sl7JmCrFcNg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J9JLsobb9iOA+TO4XT0ug/rSn8a+F85LdVXLiHZySEjGxNtCuiN6PGdAfMFnlxrQUo+EAo/epl1NV7ikvbrcIg==')})
  }
